Implications: Good and Evil, and the Conventional Example
Draws implications of the relational view and provides a conventional example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the relational view of command and prohibition implies goodness and evil in the acts, and how conventional usage further illustrates this flexibility.

Core Idea
Command indicates goodness, prohibition indicates evil, but the opposition is in the objects, not the commands themselves.

Continuing the argument, Imam al-Nasafi now draws out the implications of the relational view: a command indicates the goodness of the commanded act, and a prohibition indicates the evil of the forbidden act. He stresses that the opposition is between the implications (goodness vs. evil) and not between command and prohibition as such. He refutes those who think command and prohibition are essentially opposite like life and death, using an analogy with father and son. Finally, he provides a concrete conventional example to show how a single utterance can bear multiple command and prohibition meanings simultaneously.

Guided Path
1
Understand the implications of command and prohibition
Learn that command indicates goodness (ḥusn) of the commanded act, and prohibition indicates evil (qubḥ) of the forbidden act, and they are opposite in implication.
2
Refute the misconception of essential opposition
Read the author's strong refutation of those who think command and prohibition are essentially opposite like knowledge and ignorance or life and death.
3
Examine the father-son analogy
See how a command cannot be a command of what it prohibits, analogous to a father cannot be his own son.
4
Analyze the conventional example
Understand how a single utterance ('Zayd') can be both a command and a prohibition by convention, illustrating the relativity of command and prohibition.

Affirmation of the Modalities of Allah's Speech
The author affirms that Allah's speech is command, prohibition, news, and inquiry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's speech comprises four distinct modalities—command, prohibition, news, and inquiry—as affirmed by evidence and manifest through spoken attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is not uniform; it is command, prohibition, news, and inquiry.

The author concludes his discussion on divine speech by affirming its multiple modalities. He argues that speech can simultaneously be command, prohibition, news, and inquiry without contradiction. This lesson examines his reasoning and the evidence for this view, which refutes opposing doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its flow. Then read the English translation, noting the key terms.
Pay attention to the structure: an example, a principle, and a detailed application.
2
Identify the four aspects
Locate the words for command, prohibition, news, and inquiry in the Arabic text. Notice how they are presented as an exhaustive list.
The four terms are: أمر, نهي, خبر, استخبار.
3
Understand the logical chain
Follow the author's argument: the example shows possibility; evidence establishes reality; then the details are given.
The phrase 'فإذا قامت الدلالة' is key to the transition.
4
Reflect on the refutation
The author says the opponent's doubt is dispelled. Think about what doubt this might answer—perhaps the idea that Allah's speech cannot be multiple things at once.
5
Connect to spoken attributes
The final sentence ties the four modalities to 'spoken attributes and indicative expressions'. Consider how this bridges divine speech and revealed texts.
This reinforces the Maturidi view that Allah's speech is expressed in the Quran and other revelations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرجل: - زيد - فهم منه هذه الأشياء وكان أمرا ونهيا وخبرا واستخبارا على التفصيل الذي بينا، ولم يكن ذلك مستحيلا. فإذا قامت الدلالة على ثبوت كل كلام الله تعالى على هذا الوجه كان ذلك ثابتا حقيقة، واندفع ما ظنه الخصم شبهة. والله الموفق. فيكون كلام الله تعالى أمرا بما أمر به في حق من أمر به في الوقت الذي أمر به، ونهيا عما نهى عنه على هذا التفصيل، وإخبارا عما أخبر، واستخبارا على الوجه الذي يليق به يظهر ذلك بهذه الصفات النطقية والعبارات الدالة.
The man - Zayd - understood from it these things, and it was a command, prohibition, news, and inquiry according to the detail we explained, and that was not impossible. So when the evidence is established for the affirmation of all of Allah's speech in this manner, that is established as real, and what the opponent imagined as an illusion is repelled. And Allah is the Grantor of success. So Allah's speech is a command regarding what He commanded for whom He commanded at the time He commanded, and a prohibition regarding what He prohibited according to this detail, and news of what He informed, and an inquiry in the manner befitting Him, manifest by these spoken attributes and indicative expressions.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a definitive statement about the nature of Allah's speech. It begins by referring to a previous example (the man Zayd) to illustrate that speech can be multiple things—command, prohibition, news, inquiry—without impossibility. Then it states that when evidence establishes that all of Allah's speech is like this, it is true and refutes the opponent's doubt. The author then spells out that Allah's speech is exactly command, prohibition, news, and inquiry in their respective contexts, manifested through spoken attributes and expressions. This affirms the Maturidi position that Allah's speech is not a single undifferentiated essence but encompasses various modalities corresponding to His will and wisdom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Command and prohibition only exist when someone is being addressed at that moment.
Correction: The speech itself is real as command and prohibition even if the addressed person exists later; the modality is inherent in the speech.

Checkpoint

A) Two: command and prohibition
B) Three: command, prohibition, and news
C) Four: command, prohibition, news, and inquiry

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is real and encompasses command, prohibition, news, and inquiry, each manifested according to divine wisdom and expressed through spoken attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage teaches that Allah's speech includes inquiry (istikhbar). Since Allah knows all things, why does He ask you (e.g., 'Who created the heavens?')? How will you respond to His inquiry — not just with words, but with your heart and actions, starting today?
?
The author uses the example of a man named Zayd to show that human speech can carry multiple meanings. When you speak, do you realize your words mirror the Divine attribute of speech? How can you ensure your commands are just, your prohibitions kind, your news truthful, and your inquiries genuine? Commit to one change in your speech this week.
?
If Allah's speech is truly real as command, prohibition, news, and inquiry, then how seriously do you take His commands and prohibitions? Is there a command you have been neglecting or a prohibition you have been rationalizing? Confront yourself honestly and resolve to align your life with His speech.

Refutation of Mu'tazila's Inconsistency on Divine Speech
The author points out a contradiction in the Mu'tazila's reasoning about Allah's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the Mu'tazila's position regarding Allah's speech by comparing their arguments about divine knowledge and power.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila accept an impossibility for knowledge but reject it for speech—a clear contradiction.

The author of the Tabṣira recalls a key inconsistency in Mu'tazilī reasoning. They claim that Allah's speech cannot be eternal command and prohibition because in human experience command requires an addressee. Yet they themselves hold that Allah's knowledge and power are identical with His essence—a notion equally impossible in the witnessed realm. This passage exposes their double standard.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the logical flow.
Notice the word 'ناقضوا' (they contradicted) which sets up the charge.
2
Identify the two analogies
The Mu'tazila use an analogy with knowledge and power to claim that command and prohibition in pre-eternity is impossible. But they themselves affirm that Allah knows what He is powerful over, which is also impossible in the witnessed realm. Identify each side.
The contrast is between their acceptance of one 'impossibility' and rejection of another.
3
Reflect on the inconsistency
Ask yourself: why is the Mu'tazila's position contradictory? What does the author mean by 'utmost confusion'? Consider how this refutation strengthens the Maturidi view on divine speech.
This step connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المعتزلة ناقضوا حيث جعلوا هذا محالا اعتبارا بالعلم والقدرة، ثم يقولون : إن الله تعالى عالم بعين ما هو به قادر وهو ذاته تعالى وإن كان هذا في الشاهد محالا وأبوا علينا هذا في الأمر والنهي، وإن كان هذا في الشاهد ممكنا بل واجبا وهذا هو غاية الحيرة والجهل بالحقائق. وبالله العصمة.
Then the Mu'tazila contradicted when they considered this impossible by analogy with knowledge and power. Then they say: Indeed Allah is knowing exactly that which He is powerful over, and that is His Essence, even if this is impossible in the witnessed realm, and they refused us this concerning command and prohibition, even though this is possible, indeed necessary, in the witnessed realm. And this is the utmost confusion and ignorance of realities. And with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's inconsistency. The author states that the Mu'tazila have contradicted themselves. They consider it impossible for Allah's speech to be command and prohibition in pre-eternity because they analogize with human knowledge and power, claiming that in the witnessed realm, command and prohibition require an addressee. Yet they themselves affirm that Allah knows exactly what He is powerful over, and that this knowledge-power identity is His Essence—something impossible in the witnessed realm. They accept this impossibility for knowledge/power but reject a similar 'impossibility' for command/prohibition, even though in the witnessed realm, command and prohibition without an immediate addressee is actually possible (e.g., addressing future generations). This shows their reasoning is confused and ignorant of true realities.

Correction: But the passage shows they accept a similar 'impossibility' in their own doctrine about knowledge and power, which is equally impossible in the witnessed world. This reveals inconsistency.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does the author attribute to the Mu'tazila?
A) They affirm Allah's speech is created but deny it is command.
B) They consider it impossible for Allah's speech to be command and prohibition in pre-eternity, yet they affirm that Allah knows exactly what He is powerful over, which is also impossible in the witnessed realm.
C) They say Allah's speech is eternal but deny it is command.
D) They reject divine power but affirm divine knowledge.

Key Takeaway

?
If you were to examine your heart honestly, is there any sin or compromise you justify with a flawed analogy, while condemning the same in others? Repent now and ask Allah to grant you consistency and clarity like the righteous.

Refutation of the Third Doubt: Command and Prohibition in Pre-Eternity
Author refutes the claim that command and prohibition are impossible in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends the possibility of God's command and prohibition in pre-eternity by exposing the Mu'tazila's inconsistency and explaining the difference between originated and eternal speech.

Core Idea
Eternal divine commands do not require temporal conditions like the presence of addressees.

The Mu'tazila argued that command and prohibition cannot exist in pre-eternity because there are no addressees. The author counters by first pointing out their own inconsistency: they accept that the Qur'an addresses future generations who were non-existent at revelation. He then deepens the argument by distinguishing between originated things, which are tied to purposes, and the eternal, which is beyond such conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the translation. Notice how the author moves from accusation to proof.
The passage is long but structured; each paragraph introduces a new layer of the refutation.
2
Identify the author's main strategy
Look for the accusation of hypocrisy (tashnīʿ) at the start. See how the author turns the Mu'tazila's own reasoning against them.
The author uses the Mu'tazila's acceptance of the Qur'an addressing future people as a counterexample.
3
Examine the critique of analogy (qiyās)
The author argues that the witnessed-unseen analogy does not force the conclusion because not all witnessed attributes apply to the unseen (e.g., being a body).
This is a key methodological point in kalām.
4
Understand the distinction between originated and eternal
The author explains that originated things (like human speech) require wisdom and conditions, but the eternal (God's speech) does not depend on external purposes or the presence of addressees.
The passage ends with this point incomplete; reflect on why this distinction undermines the doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حل الشبهة الثالثة. وهي القول باستحالة الأمر والنهي في الأزل مع انعدام المكلفين استدلالا بالشاهد على ما قرروا. فهو أن يقال لهم: قد علمتم معاشر المعتزلة أن التشنيع على الخصوم بشيء يرى المشنع عين ذلك الشيء حكمة وصوابا خارجا عن عادات العقلاء، وهو يعد أفحش مناقضة وأشد انقطاع، وأنتم في هذا السؤال وإثارة هذه الشبهة سالكون هذا المسلك لازمون هذه الطريقة، وبيان هذا أن عندكم كان المنزل على النبي عليه السلام خطابا لمن يوجد من أهل الفعل إلى قيام الساعة عند البلوغ وإن كانوا معدومين حال نزول الخطاب، ولم يعد ذلك سفها ولا خروجا عن الحكمة استدلالا بالشاهد فكذا ما قلنا، ومن لم يجعل لمن وجد بعد ذلك العصر مخاطبا بذلك الخطاب مع انقطاع الوحي، أبطل الشرائع وأخرج كل الخليقة بعد وفاة النبي عن لوازم الأمر والنهي وأفلتهم عن ربقة الخطاب والقول به كفر صراح. ثم يقال لهم: إن كان هذا هكذا في الشاهد فلم ينبغي أن يكون في الغائب هكذا؟ فلابد من إثبات التسوية بين الشاهد والغائب ليمكن الاستدلال وتعدية الحكم إلى الغائب، أليس أن كل فاعل في الشاهد جسم وهو لحم ودم وعظم وعصب ولا يلزم مثله في الغائب فكذا فيما نحن فيه. ثم نكشف عن المعنى فنقول: إن الأصل أن وجود المحدث هو الذي يتعلق بالعلل والحكم، لا وجود القديم، إذ المحدث لم يكن ثم كان بتكوين غيره إياه فيتقصى عن الحكمة التي لأجلها أحدثه الصانع وأوجده. فأما ما كان لا ابتداء لوجوده وهو واجب الوجود لذاته، لم يكن وجوده متعلقا بمعنى وراء ذاته الذي هو واجب الوجود أليس أن من قال: لا حكمة في وجود صانع العالم سابقا على العالم سبقا لا نهاية له يستحق وينسب إلى الغباوة والجهل لما مر من العلة، فكذا هذا. ثم نقرر هذا الكلام فنقول بأن كلام واحد منا في الشاهد محدث يحصل باكتساب المتكلم فيطلب لوجوده جهة الحكمة، فإن كان المخاطب حاضرا موجودا
As for resolving the third doubt—which is the claim of the impossibility of command and prohibition in pre-eternity with the absence of obligated persons, by drawing analogy from the witnessed realm as they argued—it is to say to them: You, O Mu'tazila, have known that disparaging opponents with something which the disparager himself sees as wisdom and correctness in his own case is outside the customs of rational people, and it is considered the foulest contradiction and severest rupture. And you, in this question and raising this doubt, are pursuing this path and adhering to this method. The explanation is that according to you, what was sent down to the Prophet (peace be upon him) was a speech addressed to those who will exist among the people of action until the Day of Resurrection at the time of maturity, even though they were non-existent at the time of the revelation. And that was not considered foolishness nor a departure from wisdom by analogy with [the witnessed], so likewise what we said. And whoever does not consider those who exist after that generation as addressed by that speech, with the cessation of revelation, has nullified the Laws and expelled all creatures after the death of the Prophet from the obligations of command and prohibition and released them from the bond of address, and saying that is plain disbelief. Then it is said to them: If this is so in the witnessed, why should it not be so in the unseen? So it is necessary to establish equality between the witnessed and the unseen to enable analogical inference and transfer of the ruling to the unseen. Is it not that every agent in the witnessed is a body, and it is flesh, blood, bone, and nerve, and its like is not necessary for the unseen? So too in our case. Then we unveil the meaning and say: The principle is that the existence of the originated is that which is connected to causes and wisdoms, not the existence of the eternal. For the originated was not then came to be by the bringing into existence of another, so it is investigated for the wisdom for which the Maker brought it into existence. As for what has no beginning to its existence and is necessary of existence by itself, its existence is not connected to a meaning beyond its Essence which is necessary of existence. Is it not that whoever says: There is no wisdom in the existence of the Maker of the world prior to the world in an infinite priority, deserves to be attributed with stupidity and ignorance due to the cause mentioned? So likewise this. Then we confirm this speech and say: The speech of one of us in the witnessed is originated, occurring by the acquisition of the speaker, so it demands for its existence a consideration of wisdom. If the addressee is present, existing...
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is the author's refutation of the third doubt: the claim that command and prohibition cannot exist in pre-eternity because there are no addressees. The author begins by accusing the Mu'tazila of hypocrisy: they disparage opponents by pointing out a flaw, yet they themselves commit the same flaw. Specifically, they accept that the Qur'an was sent down to address people who would exist after the Prophet's time, even though they were non-existent at the time of revelation. They do not consider this foolish or unwise. So by the same logic, command and prohibition in pre-eternity should be possible. The author then warns that denying this leads to nullification of the Sharia and disbelief. Next, the author engages their analogy: if they rely on the witnessed-unseen analogy, they must apply it consistently. But not every attribute of the witnessed applies to the unseen (e.g., being a body). Therefore, the analogy does not force the conclusion that command and prohibition require a present addressee. Then the author unveils the deeper principle: originated things exist for a purpose and are connected to causes and wisdoms, but the eternal (God) is not caused or dependent on external wisdom for His existence. His speech, being eternal, does not require a temporal condition like the presence of an addressee. The argument continues, but the text cuts off midway through explaining that human speech (originated) requires wisdom for its existence, whereas God's speech does not. This concluding part is incomplete in this window.

Correction: The author shows that the Qur'anic example proves that commands can address future non-existent people, and the eternal nature of God's attributes removes the need for temporal conditions.

Resolution of the Fifth Objection: God's Eternal Speech
Resolves fifth objection by contrasting human and divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that speaking in solitude is foolish does not apply to God's eternal speech, and how it actually refutes the Mu'tazilite position.

Core Idea
God's eternal speech needs no wisdom condition, so the objection misfires.

In this passage, the author settles the fifth objection by distinguishing between created human speech, which requires a condition of wisdom, and God's eternal speech, which does not. The objection is cleverly turned back against the Mu'tazilites, who hold that God's speech is created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation to understand the argument completely. Let the author's own words guide you.
2
Identify the key distinction
Notice how the author differentiates human speech (originated, seeks wisdom) from God's speech (eternal, necessary). This distinction is the core of the resolution.
Human speech needs a good consequence to be wise; God's speech does not.
3
Understand the resolution
The objection claims speaking alone is foolish unless for recollection or dispelling loneliness. Since God's speech is eternal and not originated, this condition does not apply. The author compares it to God's essence—which also does not require a justification.
4
See the refutation of the Mu'tazilites
The author argues that the objection would only hold if God's speech were originated before hearers existed. Since the Mu'tazilites believe speech is created, the objection actually refutes them, not the orthodox position.
This is a clever polemical move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقرر هذا الكلام فنقول بأن كلام واحد منا في الشاهد محدث يحصل باكتساب المتكلم فيطلب لوجوده جهة الحكمة، فإن كان المخاطب حاضرا موجودا حصلت له العاقبة الحميدة فصار حكمة، وإن كان معدوما أو غائبا لم يتعلق به العاقبة الحميدة فكان سفها. فأما كلام الله تعالى فهو أزلي واجب الوجود فلا يطلب لثبوته في الأزل حكمة كما فى حق الذات وهذا هو حل الشبهة الخامسة، أعني قولهم: إن التكلم في الخلوة مع نفسه لن يكون إلا للتذكر أو لدفع الوحشة، والتكلم بدون ذلك سفه، إن كان هذا هكذا في حق من أحدث كلامه، فأما في حق من كان كلامه أزليا غير محدث وغير داخل تحت القدرة فلا. وإنما يستقيم هذان الكلامان أن لو كان كلامه محدثا وكان أحدثه قبل حدوث المخاطبين بأزمنة كثيرة، فيتوجه حينئذ هذا الإلزام، فيكون هذان الكلامان في الحقيقة متوجهين على المعتزلة، حيث زعموا أنه تعالى أحدث كلامه في عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطابا لمن في عصرنا ولمن يوجد إلى قيام الساعة، فأما علينا فلا.
Then we confirm this discourse and say: The speech of any one of us in the witnessed is originated, acquired by the speaker, and therefore for its existence it seeks a direction of wisdom. So if the addressee is present, existing, the good consequence is obtained for him, so it becomes wisdom. But if the addressee is non-existent or absent, the good consequence is not attached to it, so it becomes foolishness. As for the speech of God Most High, it is eternal, necessary of existence, so for its subsistence in pre-eternity it does not seek wisdom, just as in the case of the essence. And this is the resolution of the fifth objection, namely their saying: 'Speaking in solitude with oneself can only be for recollection or to dispel loneliness, and speaking without that is foolishness.' If this is the case regarding one who originates his speech, then regarding one whose speech is eternal, not originated, and not subject to power, [it is] not [so]. And these two statements would only be valid if His speech were originated and He had originated it many ages before the advent of the addressees; then this objection would apply. Thus these two statements in reality apply to the Mu'tazilites, who claim that He Most High originated His speech in the era of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as an address to those in our era and to those who exist until the Day of Resurrection. As for us, no.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is the detailed resolution of the fifth objection (al-shubha al-khamisa), which states that speaking to oneself is only for recollection or to dispel loneliness, and otherwise is foolish. The author applies the earlier principle: human speech is originated and seeks wisdom; if the addressee is absent, it lacks good consequence (al-`aqiba al-hamida) and is foolish. God's speech is eternal (azali) and necessary of existence; it does not seek wisdom for its subsistence, just as God's essence does not. Therefore the objection does not apply to God. The author then turns the objection against the Mu'tazilites, who believe God's speech is originated. If it were originated long before the addressees existed, it would indeed lack good consequence and be foolish. Thus the objection actually refutes the Mu'tazilite position, not the orthodox one.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection about speaking in solitude refutes the orthodox position that God's speech is eternal.
Correction: The author shows that the objection only applies to originated speech, so it does not affect the orthodox view of eternal speech; rather, it refutes the Mu'tazilite view of created speech.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal speech is not subject to the same conditions as created speech, so objections about wisdom do not apply.

?

?
When you read the Quran, do you approach it as the eternal speech of Allah, or as a book that needs to prove its wisdom to you? This lesson teaches that God's speech is not dependent on any condition. Will you let that truth transform how you listen to His words today?

The Second Answer: Permanence of Divine Speech
Second answer: permanence distinguishes divine speech from created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the eternity and permanence of divine speech make it wise and beneficial for all addressees, even future generations.

Core Idea
Eternal divine speech persists to benefit all addressees.

This passage provides a second answer to an objection against the divine attribute of speech. The objector claimed that addressing non-existent addressees is foolish because it lacks good consequence. The defender here shows that the key is permanence: created speech perishes and thus fails to benefit future addressees, but God's speech is eternal and remains forever, thereby attaining good consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the second answer carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first defines the criterion for wisdom and foolishness, then applies it to created speech and divine speech.
The criterion is whether speech is devoid of good consequence (al-`aqiba al-hamida).
2
Compare created and divine speech
Identify the key difference: created speech cannot persist, so it perishes before future addressees exist, making it foolish. Divine speech is eternal and cannot perish, so it remains to reach all addressees.
The conclusion hinges on the impossibility of permanence for created speech and the impossibility of non-existence for eternal speech.
3
Apply the reasoning to the Qur'an
Understand why the revelation to the Prophet was not foolish: it remains until the Day of Resurrection, thus it benefits all until then.
This also refutes the objection only against those who affirm permanence of created speech; those denying permanence are already refuted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب آخر أن ما خلا عن العاقبة الحميدة فهو سفه، وما لم يخل عنها فهو ليس بسفه، هذا هو الفصل بين السفه والحكمة عندنا، ثم الكلام المحدث مستحيل البقاء فإذا وجد به الخطاب في حال عدم المخاطب أو غيبته ينعدم لاستحالة بقائه، ولا يبقى إلى وقت وجود المخاطب لتتعلق به العاقبة الحميدة، بل خلا عنها، فكان سفها فأما كلام الله تعالى فهو أزلي فكل أزلي، مستحيل العدم على ما قررنا فيبقى إلى وقت وجود المخاطبين، فلم يخل عن العاقبة الحميدة فلم يكن سفها، ولهذا لم يكن الخطاب المنزل على النبي عليه السلام سفها وإن كان خطابا لمن يوجد إلى قيام الساعة لبقائه إلى قيام الساعة، وهذا الإلزام على القائلين منهم ببقاء ذلك الكلام، فأما المنكرون لبقائه، وقد بينا فساد ذلك بحمد الله غير مرة وتبين بالوقوف على هذه
And another answer: That which is devoid of good consequence is foolishness, and that which is not devoid of it is not foolishness. This is the distinction between foolishness and wisdom according to us. Then created speech is impossible of permanence; so if the address occurs at a time of the addressee's non-existence or absence, he becomes nonexistent due to the impossibility of its remaining, and it does not remain until the time of the addressee's existence for the good consequence to be attached to it; rather, it is devoid of it, so it is foolishness. As for the speech of God Most High, it is eternal, and everything eternal is impossible of non-existence according to what we have established. So it remains until the time of the existence of the addressees, so it is not devoid of good consequence, so it is not foolishness. For this reason, the revelation sent down to the Prophet, peace be upon him, was not foolishness, even though it is an address to those who exist until the Day of Resurrection, because it remains until the Day of Resurrection. And this objection applies to those among them who affirm the permanence of that speech. As for those who deny its permanence, we have shown the corruption of that, praise be to God, more than once, and it is evident upon examining this...
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a second answer (jawab akhar) to the objection, focusing on the property of permanence (baqa'). The author first defines the criterion: wisdom requires good consequence (al-`aqiba al-hamida); speech devoid of it is foolish. Created speech cannot persist (mustahil al-baqa'), so if it is uttered when the addressee is absent or nonexistent, it perishes before the addressee exists and thus fails to produce good consequence; hence it is foolish. In contrast, God's speech is eternal (azali), and everything eternal is impossible of non-existence; it remains forever. Therefore it does not perish and reaches all addressees, obtaining good consequence. The author then applies this to the Qur'an: the revelation to the Prophet is not foolish because it remains until Judgment Day. The objection thus only troubles those (i.e., some Mu'tazilites) who affirm the permanence of created speech, while those who deny permanence have already been refuted.

بقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Speech must be simultaneous with the addressee to be wise.
Correction: Permanence of speech allows it to benefit future addressees, as with God's eternal speech.

Checkpoint

A) Because God creates new speech for each generation.

D) Because it was revealed long after the addressees existed.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is eternal and permanent, ensuring it benefits all future generations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God's speech is eternal and remains until the Day of Resurrection. When you open the Qur'an tonight, will you receive it as a living address meant specifically for you—or as an ancient text? What will change if you truly believe it speaks to you now?
?
The passage says that speech devoid of good consequence is foolishness. Think about the words you have spoken today: will any of them produce good consequence beyond this moment? If not, will you repent and commit to speaking only what remains for benefit?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's speech has reached you across time to guide you, would you still delay acting on its commands? Name one command from the Qur'an you have been procrastinating, and resolve tonight to obey it as a direct message from the Eternal.

The Eternity of God's Speech Refutes the Fifth Objection
Al-Nasafi gives the first answer to the fifth objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that eternal speech without audience is foolish only applies to created, contingent speech, not to God's eternal speech.

Core Idea
God's eternal speech does not require the purposes of human speech.

The fifth objection claims that speaking in solitude is only for recollection or dispelling loneliness; otherwise it is foolish. Al-Nasafi begins his refutation by distinguishing created speech from God's eternal speech. He shows that this objection only applies if speech is created, and then turns it against the Mu'tazila who believe God's speech was created in time.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read the Arabic from 'فأما كلام الله تعالى' up to the point where Al-Nasafi says this objection is really against the Mu'tazila. Follow the translation closely.
Notice how Al-Nasafi directly contrasts created speech with eternal speech.
2
Understand the principle: eternal speech needs no purpose
Reflect on why God's speech, being eternal and necessary, does not require a wisdom (hikma) for its existence, unlike created speech which requires a purpose.
3
See how the objection boomerangs on the Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi argues that if speech were created long before the addressees, the objection would apply. The Mu'tazila claim God created speech in the Prophet's time, but earlier speech would be pointless.
This exposes a flaw in the Mu'tazila's own position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حصلت له العاقبة الحميدة فصار ،حكمة، وإن كان معدوما أو غائبا لم يتعلق به (۱) العاقبة الحميدة) (۲) فكان سفها. فأما كلام الله تعالى فهو أزلي واجب الوجود فلا يطلب لثبوته في الأزل حكمة كما فى حق الذات وهذا هو حل الشبهة الخامسة، أعني قولهم: إن التكلم في الخلوة مع نفسه لن يكون إلا للتذكر أو لدفع الوحشة، والتكلم (۳) بدون ذلك سفه، إن كان هذا هكذا في حق من أحدث كلامه، فأما في حق من كان كلامه أزليا غير محدث وغير داخل تحت القدرة فلا. وإنما يستقيم هذان الكلامان أن لو كان كلامه محدثا ، وكان أحدثه قبل حدوث المخاطبين بأزمنة كثيرة، فيتوجه حينئذ هذا الإلزام، فيكون هذان الكلامان في الحقيقة متوجهين على المعتزلة، حيث زعموا أنه تعالى أحدث كلامه في عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطابا لمن(4) في عصرنا ولمن يوجد إلى قيام الساعة، فأما علينا فلا
وجواب :آخر أن ما خلا عن العاقبة الحميدة فهو سفه، وما لم يخل عنها فهو ليس بسفه، هذا هو الفصل بين السفه والحكمة عندنا ، ثم الكلام المحدث مستحيل البقاء فإذا وجد به الخطاب في حال عدم المخاطب أو غيبته ينعدم لاستحالة بقائه، ولا يبقى إلى وقت وجود المخاطب لتتعلق به العاقبة الحميدة، بل خلا عنها، فكان سفها فأما كلام الله تعالى فهو أزلي فكل أزلي، مستحيل العدم على ما قررنا فيبقى إلى وقت وجود المخاطبين، فلم يخل عن العاقبة الحميدة فلم يكن سفها، ولهذا لم يكن الخطاب المنزل (۹) على النبي عليه السلام سفها وإن كان خطابا لمن يوجد إلى قيام الساعة لبقائه إلى قيام الساعة، وهذا الإلزام على القائلين منهم ببقاء ذلك الكلام، فأما المنكرون لبقائه، وقد بينا فساد ذلك بحمد الله غير مرة وتبين بالوقوف على هذه الجملة دهاء هذه الشبهة، وعدول (۱) المعتزلة عند تمسكهم بها عن مراعاة شرائط صحة الاستدلال بالشاهد على الغائب. والله ولي التوفيق.
The good consequence resulted for him, so it became wisdom, and if [the speech] was non-existent or absent, the good consequence would not attach to it, so it would be foolishness. As for the speech of Allah the Exalted, it is eternal, necessary of existence, so one does not seek for its establishment in eternity a wisdom as in the case of the Essence. This is the resolution of the fifth doubt, namely their saying: 'Speaking in solitude with oneself can only be for recollection or to dispel loneliness, and speaking without that is foolishness.' If this is so in the case of one who creates his speech, then as for the case of one whose speech is eternal, not created, and not under power, it is not so. These two statements would only be valid if His speech were created, and He created it many ages before the existence of the addressees, then this objection would apply. So these two statements are in reality directed against the Mu'tazila, since they claim that He the Exalted created His speech in the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a discourse to those in our era and to those who exist until the Day of Resurrection. But as for us, it is not.

Another answer: That which is devoid of good consequence is foolishness, and that which is not devoid of it is not foolishness. This is the distinction between foolishness and wisdom according to us. Then created speech is impossible of remaining, so if discourse occurs by it in the state of the addressee's non-existence or absence, it ceases to exist due to the impossibility of its remaining, and it does not remain until the time of the addressee's existence for the good consequence to attach to it. Rather, it is devoid of it, so it would be foolishness. As for the speech of Allah the Exalted, it is eternal, and every eternal thing is impossible of non-existence, as we established, so it remains until the time of the addressees' existence. Thus it is not devoid of good consequence, so it is not foolishness. For this reason, the revealed discourse upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) was not foolishness, even though it was a discourse to those who exist until the Day of Resurrection, because it remains until the Day of Resurrection. And this objection is against those among them who affirm the remaining of that speech. As for those who deny its remaining, we have shown the corruption of that, praise be to Allah, more than once, and it becomes clear by reflecting on this passage the subtlety of this doubt, and the deviation of the Mu'tazila in their adherence to it from observing the conditions for the validity of analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage refutes the fifth objection raised by opponents regarding the eternity of God's speech (kalam). The objection claims that speaking in solitude (khilwa) is only for recollection or dispelling loneliness; otherwise it is foolishness (safah). Al-Nasafi first establishes that this reasoning applies only to created, contingent speech, not to God's eternal speech which is necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud) and does not require a purpose like human speech. He then provides two distinct answers. The first answer turns the objection back on the Mu'tazila, who claim that God created speech at the time of the Prophet. If God's speech were created long before the addressees, the objection would apply to them. The second answer defines foolishness as that which lacks a good consequence (al-‘āqiba al-ḥamīda). Created speech cannot remain and thus cannot achieve a good consequence when addressed to non-existent beings, but God's eternal speech remains until the addressees exist, thereby securing the good consequence. Al-Nasafi concludes by criticizing the Mu'tazila's faulty analogical reasoning (istidlal bi al-shahid ‘ala al-gha’ib).

Key Terms
كلام الله
أزلي
محدث
سفه
حكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's speech must have a purpose like human speech because it is spoken.
Correction: God's speech is eternal and necessary; it does not require a purpose for its existence, unlike temporal created speech.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, why does the objection about foolishness not apply to God's speech?
A) Because God never speaks alone.
B) Because God's speech is eternal and does not require a purpose like created speech.
C) Because God's speech is created at the same time as the addressees.
D) Because the Mu'tazila agree with the objection.

Key Takeaway
The objection that eternal speech is foolish only works for created speech, not for God's eternal speech which is necessary and requires no external purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you treat it as a message that has a purpose only for your moment, or as the eternal speech of Allah? How would your heart tremble differently if you truly believed it has been His speech from eternity without needing you?
?
The Mu'tazila accused the orthodox of believing in foolishness because they measured Allah by human standards. Where in your own life do you subconsciously measure Allah's actions or commands by human logic, expecting them to fit your understanding of purpose and wisdom?
?
If you truly internalized that Allah's speech is necessary and not created, what would change about the weight you give to His words when they contradict your desires?

Good Consequence Distinguishes Wisdom from Foolishness
Al-Nasafi gives the second answer defining foolishness and applying it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi defines foolishness as that which lacks a good consequence, and why created speech cannot achieve it while eternal speech does.

Core Idea
Foolishness is lack of good consequence; eternal speech secures it.

Al-Nasafi provides a second answer based on the definition of foolishness and wisdom. He argues that created speech cannot persist to produce a good consequence, but God's eternal speech remains until the addressees exist, thereby achieving wisdom. This also explains why the revealed Quran is not foolish.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
From 'وجواب آخر' to the end. Notice the definition of foolishness and how it applies to created vs. eternal speech.
2
Understand the definition: foolishness = lacking good consequence
Al-Nasafi states that wisdom and foolishness are distinguished by whether the action leads to a good outcome. This is a key criterion.
3
Apply to created speech: it perishes, so can't have good consequence
Created speech cannot remain; if addressed to non-existent beings, it disappears before they exist, so it lacks good consequence and is foolish.
4
Apply to eternal speech: it remains, so good consequence is achieved
God's speech is eternal and impossible of non-existence, so it persists until the addressees come, obtaining the good consequence.
5
See the implication for the Quran
The revealed Quran is eternal speech (in its essence) and remains until the Day of Resurrection, so it is not foolish.

Refutation of the Fourth Objection: Pre-Eternal Reports Are Not False
Al-Nasafi refutes the fourth objection about pre-eternal reports being false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the claim that God's pre-eternal reports about future events would be false, using a prophetic hadith as evidence.

Core Idea
God's past-tense reports about future events are true because His knowledge encompasses all time.

The fourth objection against God's attributes argues that the Qur'an contains past-tense verses about future events, making them false. Al-Nasafi responds by citing a prophetic hadith that reported future signs long before they occurred, demonstrating that such reports are not false but true by God's foreknowledge. This lesson examines both the objection and the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the initial part of the passage that outlines the fourth doubt about pre-eternal reports. Notice the examples from the Qur'an (Adam, Abraham, Moses, Pharaoh) and the reasoning that past-tense reports about not-yet-occurred events would be false.
2
Identify the refutation
Al-Nasafi's answer is to cite a prophetic hadith that reported future events (signs of the Hour) long before they occurred, yet it is considered true. See how this example counters the objection.
The hadith is transmitted by tawatur, indicating its authenticity.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this refutation works: because God's knowledge makes future events certain, the use of the past tense indicates certainty, not temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حل الشبهة الرابعة وهي أن الإخبار في الأزل عن عصيان آدم عليه السلام بقوله تعالى: وَعَصَى ءَادَمُ رَبَّهُ، فَغَوَى ) (۲) و عن قول إبراهيم عليه السلام بقوله : وَإِذْ قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ رَبِّ اجْعَلْ هَذَا الْبَلَدَ آمِنًا (۳) وعن إلقاء موسى عليه السلام العصا بقوله تعالى : فَأَلْقَى عَصَاهُ (٤) وإرائه فرعون الآية بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَرَنهُ ﴿ الآية الكبرى (٥) وعن وجود أفعال كثيرة من فرعون بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَكَذَّبَ وَعَصَى ثُمَّ أَدْبَرَ يَسْعَى فَحَشَرَ فَنَادَى فَقَالَ أَنَا رَبُّكُمُ الْأَعْلَى ) : (٦) في نظائر (۷) لها كثيرة قبل وجود هذه الأفعال، يكون كذبا إذ كل ذلك إخبار عن الماضي، وهذه (۸) الأفعال قبل وجودها ما كانت ماضية، والكذب على الله تعالى محال.
(٢٢)
فهو أن يقال : أليس أن المروي على طريق الاستفاضة ثابت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه
(۱
قال "أشراط الساعة منعت العراق قفيزها (۱) ودرهمها، ومنعت الشام إردبَّها (١٠) ولم يوجد .بعد وقال عليه السلام هذا القول قبل هذا بقريب من خمسمائة سنة.
As for the resolution of the fourth doubt, which is that pre-eternal informing about the disobedience of Adam (peace be upon him) by His saying: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord, so he went astray' (20:121), and about the saying of Abraham (peace be upon him) by His saying: 'And when Abraham said, "My Lord, make this city secure"' (14:35), and about the throwing of Moses (peace be upon him) of the staff by His saying: 'Then he threw his staff' (7:107), and His showing Pharaoh the sign by His saying: 'So he showed him the great sign' (79:20), and about the existence of many actions of Pharaoh by His saying: 'So he denied and disobeyed, then turned away striving. Then he gathered and called out, saying, "I am your Lord, the Most High"' (79:21-24), and their many parallels, before the existence of these actions, would be false, since all that is informing about the past, and these actions before their existence were not past, and falsehood concerning Allah the Exalted is impossible.

(22) So it is to be said: Is it not that what is transmitted by widespread transmission is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'The signs of the Hour: Iraq will withhold its qafiz and its dirham, and Syria will withhold its irdabb,' and it has not occurred yet. And he (peace be upon him) said this saying about nearly five hundred years before this.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage refutes the fourth doubt (shubha) concerning God's pre-eternal reports (akhbar) about future events. The objection argues that the Qur'an contains past-tense verses reporting events like Adam's disobedience, Abraham's prayer, Moses' staff, and Pharaoh's actions, which were revealed before those events occurred. Since they are in the past tense but the events had not happened, they would be false (kidhb), and falsehood is impossible for God. Al-Nasafi answers by citing a prophetic hadith transmitted by widespread transmission (tawatur) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) reported future signs of the Hour (like Iraq withholding its qafiz and dirham) about five hundred years before they occurred, yet it is true. This demonstrates that past-tense reports about future events are not false because God's knowledge encompasses all times, and the past tense can be used for what is decreed or known to occur inevitably. The example of the hadith shows the validity of such reports.

Key Terms
إخبار
أزل
كذب
مروي
استفاضة
شبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's past-tense reports about future events are false because the events had not occurred at the time of revelation.
Correction: They are true because God's knowledge makes future events certain, and the past tense indicates certainty, not temporal past.

Checkpoint
How does al-Nasafi answer the fourth objection that God's pre-eternal reports about future events would be false?
A) He denies that God uses past tense for future events.
B) He cites a prophetic hadith about future signs that was true despite being reported long before.
C) He says that God's reports are not in the past tense.
D) He claims that the events were already past in God's knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Pre-eternal reports about future events are not false because God's knowledge makes them certain, as shown by the Prophet's hadith about the signs of the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a promise from Allah in the Qur'an that has not yet been fulfilled, do you live with the same certainty as if it had already happened? What is one area where your actions do not reflect that certainty?
?
The doubt about past-tense reports arises from applying human limitations to Allah. Where in your life do you constrain your understanding of Allah's attributes by your own experience?
?
The Prophet ﷺ spoke about the signs of the Hour as if they had already happened, because he knew Allah's decree is certain. Do you treat Allah's decrees—both the ones you know and the ones you don't—as absolutely certain? What would change if you did?

The Pillar Analogy: Why Divine Reports Remain True Through Time
Demonstrative proof using pillar analogy for divine reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the pillar analogy illustrates that divine reports and knowledge are immutable while the objects of knowledge change.

Core Idea
Change is in the objects, not in God's knowledge or reports.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful demonstrative argument against the objection that divine reports would change if they speak of things that pass from future to past. He distinguishes between the report itself and what it reports about, showing that only the latter undergoes temporal change. A simple analogy of a pillar and a moving observer makes this clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: first the claim about reports, then knowledge, then the pillar analogy.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three temporal states
The author describes three scenarios for the reported thing: future (does not exist yet), present (exists), and past (has passed). Observe how the report remains unchanged in each case.
3
Understand the parallel with knowledge
The author applies the same logic to God's knowledge: knowledge of a thing before its existence, during, and after does not change; only the known object changes.
This reinforces the immutability of divine attributes.
4
Reflect on the pillar analogy
Imagine a stationary pillar. A person's orientation relative to it changes (front, back, right, left), but the pillar itself remains unchanged. This illustrates that change is relative to the observer, not the object.
Apply this to the case of divine reports: the report is like the pillar, and temporal states are like the observer's positions.
5
Connect to the overall argument
This demonstrative answer refutes the objection that God's reports would change over time. The report stays true regardless of when its content occurs.
The author also mentions that previous doubts have been resolved elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الجواب البرهاني أن يقال : إن إخبار الله تعالى إخبار عن المخبرات بأحوالهم وأوصافها ، فإذا لم يوجد مخبره وجب علينا القول بأنه خبر عنه أنه يكون وإذا وجد مخبره، وجب القول إنه خبر أنه ثابت، وإذا انعدم ومضى وجب القول إنه خبر عنه أنه كان والتغير على المخبر عنه لا على الخبر دليله ما تلونا من الآيات. وكذا علمه تعالى بالمعلومات، فإن علم الله تعالى بوجود آدم عليه السلام قبل وجوده علم بأنه يوجد، وبعدما وجد علم بأنه موجود و بعد انقراضه علم بأنه كان، وكذا في كل موجود على التغير ولا تغير على العلم عندنا، ولا على الذات الذي علم به عند المعتزلة، إنما التغير على المعلوم فكذا في الخبر، ونظيره في المشاهدات الأسطوانة المنصوبة إذا توجه إليها إنسان كانت قدامه، وإذا حول ظهره إليها كانت خلفه، وإذا حول يمينه إليها كانت عن يمينه، وإذا حول يساره إليها كانت عن يساره، ولا تغير عليها إنما التغير على هذا الإنسان. فكذا فيما نحن فيه. وقد مر حل الشبهة الخامسة في حل الشبهة الثالثة، وحل الشبهة السادسة في حل الشبهة الأولى (وقد تقصينا عن حل الشبهة العقلية بحمد الله تعالى).
Then the demonstrative answer is to say: Indeed, the report of God Almighty is a report about the reported things with their states and attributes. So if its reported thing does not exist, we must say that it is a report that it will be; if its reported thing exists, we must say that it is a report that it is; if it is absent and has passed, we must say that it is a report that it was. And change is upon the reported thing, not upon the report, as evidence from the verses we have recited. And likewise His knowledge, Exalted, of the known things. For God's knowledge of the existence of Adam, peace be upon him, before his existence is knowledge that he will exist; after he exists, it is knowledge that he exists; and after his extinction, it is knowledge that he was. And likewise for every existent with change. There is no change in knowledge according to us, nor in the essence by which He knows according to the Mu'tazila; rather change is in the known. So too with the report. An analogy in observable things is a standing pillar: when a person faces it, it is in front of him; when he turns his back to it, it is behind him; when he turns to his right, it is to his right; when he turns to his left, it is to his left. There is no change in it; rather change is in this person. So too in our case. And the solution of the fifth doubt has passed in the solution of the third doubt, and the solution of the sixth doubt in the solution of the first, and we have fully treated the rational doubts by the praise of God Almighty.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This is a demonstrative (burhani) answer. The author distinguishes between the report (khabar) and the reported thing (mukhbar), and between knowledge ('ilm) and the known (ma'lum). He argues that change occurs only in the object, not in the report or knowledge itself. He then provides an analogy: a pillar remains unchanged while a person's orientation relative to it changes. This illustrates that God's knowledge and reports are immutable; what changes is the temporal state of the created objects. The passage also notes that previous doubts have been resolved.

إخبار
مخبر عنه
علم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine reports must change when the events they describe move from future to past.
Correction: Change occurs in the reported object, not in the report itself. The report remains true regardless of temporal state.

Checkpoint
According to the demonstrative answer, what changes when a reported event passes from future to past?
A) The report itself
B) The reported thing
C) God's knowledge
D) The essence of God

Key Takeaway
Divine reports and knowledge are immutable; temporal change affects only the created objects of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider your own life: You have a past full of sins, a present with struggles, and a future unknown. Do you truly believe that God's knowledge of you—every moment—never changes, and that His decree about you is fixed? How does this belief affect your fear of His judgment and your hope for His mercy? Will you ever use your changing moods or circumstances as an excuse to doubt His unchanging truth?
?
The pillar analogy shows that when you change your position, the pillar appears different even though it is unchanged. In your relationship with God, have you sometimes thought that God was distant or angry because you felt far from Him, when in reality He is fixed and it is you who have moved? What step will you take today to 'turn back' and realign your orientation to His unchanging reality?
?
God's report about Adam before, during, and after his existence is true. What does this imply about God's knowledge of your own beginning, your current state, and your end? How should this shape your attitude towards your past mistakes and your future hopes—do you trust that His promise of forgiveness is as certain as His knowledge?

God's Report and Knowledge Remain Unchanged by Temporal Events
Nasafi proves that God's report and knowledge are not changed by the passage of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's report and knowledge remain unchanged despite changes in the objects they refer to, and how Nasafi uses logical reasoning and analogy to defend this doctrine.

Core Idea
God's knowledge and speech are unchanging; only the known objects change.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key theological challenge: if God speaks about future events, does His speech change when those events occur? Nasafi demonstrates that change applies only to the reported objects, not to God's attributes of speech or knowledge. He grounds his argument in Quranic verses and an everyday analogy, defending the orthodox position against those who might infer imperfection in God.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening lines where opponents claim past events have passed. Nasafi poses a dilemma about Quranic verses reporting events.
Notice the dilemma forces opponents to either reject the Quran or accept its truth.
2
Follow the demonstrative answer
The passage explains how God's report relates to objects in three temporal states: before, during, and after existence. Identify the three cases.
Change is on the reported thing, not the report.
3
Apply the same logic to knowledge
Nasafi applies the same reasoning to God's knowledge, using Adam as an example. Observe how knowledge of Adam before, during, and after his life remains unchanged.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite view that knowledge changes.
4
Learn from the analogy
Read the pillar analogy about a standing pillar and a moving person. Understand how the pillar's relation changes but the pillar itself does not.
Analogize to God's report/knowledge: the object's relation to time changes, but the attribute does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: نعم كل ذلك قد مضى. قيل: أكذب هذه الآيات أم لا ؟ فإن قالوا: لا أبطلوا دليلهم وإن قالوا: نعم. كفروا . ثم (١) الجواب البرهاني أن يقال : إن (٢) إخبار الله تعالى إخبار عن المخبرات بأحوالهم وأوصافها ، فإذا لم يوجد مخبره وجب علينا القول بأنه خبر عنه أنه يكون وإذا وجد مخبره، وجب القول إنه خبر أنه ثابت، وإذا انعدم ومضى وجب القول إنه خبر عنه أنه كان والتغير على المخبر عنه لا على الخبر دليله ما تلونا من الآيات. وكذا علمه تعالى بالمعلومات، فإن علم الله تعالى بوجود آدم عليه السلام قبل وجوده علم بأنه يوجد، وبعدما وجد علم بأنه موجود و بعد انقراضه علم بأنه كان، وكذا في كل موجود على التغير ولا تغير على العلم عندنا، ولا على الذات الذي علم به عند المعتزلة، إنما التغير على المعلوم فكذا في الخبر، ونظيره (٣) في المشاهدات الأسطوانة المنصوبة إذا توجه إليها إنسان كانت قدامه، وإذا حول ظهره إليها كانت خلفه، وإذا حول يمينه إليها كانت عن يمينه، وإذا حول يساره إليها كانت عن يساره، ولا تغير عليها إنما التغير على هذا الإنسان. فكذا فيما نحن فيه.
If they say: 'Yes, all that has passed.' It is said: 'Do you declare these verses false or not?' If they say: 'No,' they invalidate their proof. If they say: 'Yes,' they disbelieve. Then the demonstrative answer is to say: Indeed, the information (khabar) of God Most High is information about the reported things (mukhbarat) regarding their states and attributes. So if its reported thing does not exist, we must say that it is news about it that it will be. And if its reported thing exists, we must say that it is news that it is established. And if it ceases and passes, we must say that it is news about it that it was. Change is upon the reported thing, not upon the report. Its evidence is the verses we have recited. Likewise, His knowledge Most High of known things. For God's knowledge of the existence of Adam, peace be upon him, before his existence is knowledge that he will exist; after he existed, knowledge that he exists; and after his extinction, knowledge that he was. And likewise for every existent, change occurs, but there is no change upon knowledge according to us, nor upon the essence by which He knows according to the Mu'tazila; change is only upon the known. So likewise in the report. Its analogy in observable things is a standing pillar: if a person faces it, it is in front of him; if he turns his back to it, it is behind him; if he turns his right side to it, it is to his right; if he turns his left side to it, it is to his left. There is no change upon it; change is only upon this person. Thus it is in our case.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's report (khabar) and knowledge (ilm) are not subject to change, even when the objects reported or known change over time. The author begins by presenting an objection from opponents: they affirm that past events have passed. He then poses a dilemma: do they declare the verses (that report future events) false or not? If they say no, their proof is invalidated; if they say yes, they disbelieve. The demonstrative answer follows: God's information is about the states of the reported things. When the reported thing does not yet exist, the report is that it will be; when it exists, the report is that it is; when it has passed, the report is that it was. Change occurs on the reported thing, not on the report. The same applies to God's knowledge: knowledge of Adam before his existence is knowledge that he will exist; after existence, knowledge that he exists; after extinction, knowledge that he was. Change is only on the known object, not on the knowledge or the divine essence (contra the Mu'tazila who posit change in the essence). The author then provides an analogy from observable experience: a standing pillar does not change when a person moves around it; only the person's relation to it changes. Similarly, God's report and knowledge remain unchanged; change is only in the temporal realities of the objects.

Key Terms
خبر
علم
مخبر
معلوم
تغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because God's speech refers to future events that later become past, the speech itself must change.
Correction: Nasafi shows that God's report and knowledge are immutable; only the reported objects and known things undergo change.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when a future event is reported in the Quran, how does God's report relate to that event before it occurs?
A) The report changes when the event occurs.
B) The report is that the event will be.
C) The report is that the event is non-existent.
D) The report is that the event was.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of speech and knowledge are eternally unchanging; only the objects they refer to undergo temporal change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge of your every sin was eternally present before Him, and He still sent you the Quran, does that not make each verse a direct call to you? How does it change the way you approach the commands and prohibitions you read?
?
The pillar analogy shows that as you move, your relation to the pillar changes, but the pillar is unmoved. Reflect: Which aspect of your life are you treating as the moving pillar—thinking that your changing circumstances alter God's truth? What would it mean to let the unchanging truth of His speech anchor you instead?
?
You have just learned that God's speech about past events is the same as His speech about future events. When you read the stories of prophets in the Quran, do you realize that God's 'news' about them is as present now as it was when first revealed? How might this reality transform your reading of those stories from mere history into a living dialogue with the One who speaks them?

Interpreting 'Amr' in the Quran
Imam Nasafi explains the verse 'And the command of Allah is done' as referring to punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Nasafi interprets 'amr' in the verse as 'affairs' or 'punishment' rather than the divine attribute of speech.

Core Idea
The word 'amr' in the Quran can mean 'affair' or 'punishment', not always 'command as speech'.

Imam Nasafi addresses a potential misunderstanding about a Quranic verse. He clarifies that when Allah says 'And the command of Allah is done', the word 'amr' does not refer to His eternal speech, but to His decree or punishment. This is a key point in defending the uncreatedness of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the poet's line and how it is used as evidence.
The poet's usage shows 'amr' can mean 'affairs'.
2
Identify the key term
Focus on the word 'amr'. What does it usually mean in theological discussions? How does Nasafi argue it means something different here?
3
Understand the theological stakes
Why is this interpretation important? If 'amr' here meant speech, it could imply the Quran is created. Nasafi's interpretation protects the belief that the Quran is uncreated.
4
Analyze the poetic evidence
Consider why Nasafi quotes a poet. What function does this serve in his argument?
Poetry is used as a linguistic witness to establish meaning.
5
Reflect and apply
Think of other Quranic verses where 'amr' might be interpreted similarly. How does this lesson affect your understanding of divine attributes?
This connects to broader discussions in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتأويل قوله تعالى: وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللهِ مَفْعُولًا قال الشاعر: فقلت لهـا أمـري إلى الله كله وإني إليه في الإياب لراجع أي شئوني وأفعالي، ولم يرد به أمره الذي هو كلامه. والله الموفق.
And the interpretation of His saying: 'And the command of Allah is done.' The poet said: 'So I said to her: my command is entirely to Allah, and I will return to Him.' Meaning my affairs and my actions, and He did not intend by it His command which is His speech. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage provides an interpretation of the Quranic verse 'And the command of Allah is done' (Quran 33:37). Imam Nasafi argues that 'amr' here does not refer to the divine attribute of speech (the eternal command), but rather to Allah's decree, punishment, or affairs. He supports this by quoting a poet who says 'my command is to Allah,' meaning my affairs and actions. Thus, the word 'amr' can mean 'affair' or 'punishment', not the eternal speech. This is a defensive argument against opponents who might use such verses to claim that the Quran (as speech) is subject to being 'done' or created.

Key Terms
أمر (amr)
تأويل (interpretation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'amr' in the verse always refers to the divine attribute of speech (the eternal command).
Correction: Imam Nasafi shows that 'amr' can mean 'affair' or 'punishment', as evidenced by Arabic usage, thus the verse does not imply that Allah's speech is created.

Checkpoint
In the verse 'Wa kana amr Allahi maf'ula', what does Imam Nasafi interpret 'amr' to mean?
A) The eternal speech of Allah
B) Allah's affairs or punishment
C) The Quran
D) A specific command

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi shows that 'amr' in the verse means 'affair' or 'punishment', not the eternal speech, defending the uncreated Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever assume you already know the meaning of a word, only to find out later that scholars interpret it differently? How will you guard against the pride of your own understanding and humbly seek the guidance of the scholars?
?
This lesson shows that even one word, misunderstood, can lead to a serious theological error. In your own life, where might a small misunderstanding or a loosely-held assumption be leading you away from the truth? Will you examine it today?
?
Imam Nasafi used poetry to clarify the Quran's meaning. What resources or people has Allah placed in your life to help you understand His book correctly? Are you using them, or are you relying on your own reading? Commit to one concrete step to deepen your understanding of a verse you think you already know.

The Quran as Uncreated Attribute
Imam Nasafi argues that the Quran is the uncreated attribute of speech, refuting alternative views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that the Quran, as an attribute of Allah, is uncreated, while its physical expressions (letters and sounds) are created.

Core Idea
The Quran's eternal attribute is uncreated; its recited words are created.

This passage from Imam Nasafi clarifies a crucial theological distinction: the Quran, as the attribute of speech subsisting in Allah's essence, is eternal and uncreated. However, the physical letters and sounds that we recite are created. Nasafi critiques both the Mu'tazila and the Hanabila for blurring this distinction, offering a clear Maturidi position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words come through.
Notice the concise style and the use of key terms like 'صفة القائمة بالذات'.
2
Identify the three groups mentioned
Find the Mu'tazila, the Hanabila, and the Hashwiyya. Understand each group's position on the Quran as reported by Nasafi.
The Mu'tazila say the Quran is created; Hanabila say the letters and sounds are uncreated; Hashwiyya say their own recitation is uncreated.
3
Focus on the critique of the Hanabila
Read carefully why Nasafi dismisses the Hanabila view. He calls it 'manifest nonsense' (هذيان ظاهر). Ask why he rejects it.
The distinction: the attribute is uncreated, but the physical expression is created.
4
Reflect on the core distinction
Summarize the lesson: the eternal attribute of speech is uncreated, but the physical recitation (letters, sounds) is created. This is the Maturidi position.
This distinction avoids both the Mu'tazili error of making the attribute created and the Hashwiyya error of making the recitation uncreated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعرف بهذه الدلائل أن القرآن غير مخلوق، وأعني به الصفة القائمة بالذات وهي الكلام. وما يدعيه المعتزلة حدوثه فهو محدث كما زعموا، ومساعدتنا إياهم على ذلك تغنيهم عن إقامة الدليل عليه. وبمعرفة حقيقة المذهب يتبين أنهم يتكلمون في المسألة في غير محال النزاع، وإنما ذلك دليل لهم على الحنابلة القائلين: إن كلام الله تعالى هو الحروف المؤلفة والأصوات المقطعة، وأنه حال في الألسنة والمصاحف والصدور وأنه مع هذا غير مخلوق. وكثير من الحشوية يساعدونهم ويقولون: لفظي بالقرآن غير مخلوق، فيجعلون قراءتهم غير مخلوقة، وهذا هذيان ظاهر.
And it is known by these evidences that the Quran is uncreated, and by it I mean the attribute subsisting in the essence, which is speech. And what the Mu'tazila claim of its temporality is temporally originated as they have alleged. And our agreeing with them on that would suffice them from establishing proof for it. And by knowing the reality of the doctrine, it becomes clear that they are speaking about the matter outside the point of contention. Rather, that is evidence for them against the Hanabila who say: Indeed, the speech of Allah, exalted is He, is the composed letters and segmented sounds, and that it inheres in tongues, mushafs, and chests, and that it is nevertheless uncreated. And many of the Hashwiyya agree with them and say: My utterance of the Quran is uncreated, thus making their recitation uncreated. And this is manifest nonsense.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument establishing that the Quran is uncreated. Imam Nasafi first states that the previous evidences prove the Quran is uncreated, clarifying that he means the attribute of speech that subsists in Allah's essence. Then he critiques the Mu'tazila who claim the Quran is created (hadith). He notes that if Muslims agreed with them on that claim, the Mu'tazila would not need to provide proof—but Muslims reject this. Next, he points out that the Mu'tazila are actually arguing against the Hanabila, who believe that Allah's speech consists of actual letters and sounds that exist in tongues, mushafs, and chests, yet are still uncreated. Imam Nasafi dismisses this view as misguided. He also criticizes the Hashwiyya who say 'my utterance of the Quran is uncreated,' thereby deifying their own recitation. He calls this 'manifest nonsense' (hudhyan zahir). Thus, his position is clear: the Quran as an attribute is uncreated, but the physical expressions (letters, sounds, recitations) are created.

Key Terms
صفة القائمة بالذات (attribute subsisting in essence)
مخلوق (created)
محدث (temporally originated)
حروف وأصوات (letters and sounds)
هذيان (nonsense)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that reciting the Quran (the physical words) is uncreated because the Quran itself is uncreated.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that only the attribute of speech in Allah's essence is uncreated; the recited letters and sounds are created.

Checkpoint
What is the position of the Hanabila regarding Allah's speech?
A) It is created
B) It is composed of letters and sounds that are uncreated
C) It is only an attribute without letters
D) It is the same as the recitation

Key Takeaway
The Quran as an eternal divine attribute is uncreated, but its physical recitation in letters and sounds is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever feel that your own voice and pronunciation are somehow divine? How does Nasafi's sharp distinction between the eternal attribute and your created recitation challenge that feeling? Will you now pause before each recitation to consciously remind yourself that you are uttering something created that points to the Uncreated?
?
Nasafi calls the belief that 'my utterance of the Quran is uncreated' manifest nonsense. Have you ever, even unconsciously, thought that your Quran recitation has a special uncreated status? If you are honest, what does that reveal about your need to 'claim' something from Allah's attribute as your own? Can you today repent of seeking honor by attributing eternity to your own actions?
?
Consider the Mu'tazila and the Hanabila: one says the Quran is fully created, the other says even the letters are uncreated. Both are wrong according to Nasafi. Which error are you more prone to—draining the Quran of its divine weight by treating it as ordinary speech, or idolizing its physical form? What one concrete step will you take this week to correct that imbalance in your heart?
